<a href="/wiki/Giudecca" title="Giudecca">Giudecca</a> canal. View from <a href="/wiki/St_Mark%27s_Campanile" title="St Mark's Campanile">St Mark's Campanile</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/220px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/330px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/440px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sandolo in a picture of <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Monti" title="Paolo Monti">Paolo Monti</a> of 1965. Fondo Paolo Monti, <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_europea_di_informazione_e_cultura" title="Biblioteca europea di informazione e cultura">BEIC</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice is built on an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of 117 islands formed by 177 canals in a shallow lagoon, connected by 409 bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In the old centre, the canals serve the function of roads, and almost every form of transport is on water or on foot. In the 19th century, a causeway to the mainland brought the <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_railway_station" title="Venezia Santa Lucia railway station">Venezia Santa Lucia railway station</a> to Venice, and the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Libert%C3%A0" title="Ponte della Libertà">Ponte della Libertà</a> road causeway and parking facilities (in Tronchetto island and in piazzale Roma) were built during the 20th century. Beyond the road and rail land entrances at the northern edge of the city, transportation within the city remains (as it was in centuries past) entirely on water or on foot. Venice is Europe's largest urban <a href="/wiki/Auto-free_zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Auto-free zones">car-free area</a>. Venice is unique in Europe, in having remained a sizable functioning city in the 21st century entirely without motorcars or trucks.</p>
<p>The classical Venetian boat is the <a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">gondola</a>, (plural: gondole) although it is now mostly used for tourists, or for weddings, funerals, or other ceremonies, or as 'traghetti' (sing.: traghetto) to cross the Canale Grande in the absence of a nearby bridge. Many gondolas are lushly appointed with crushed velvet seats and Persian rugs. Less well-known is the smaller <a href="/wiki/Sandolo" title="Sandolo">sandolo</a>. At the front of each gondola that works in the city, there is a large piece of metal called the <i>fèro</i> (iron). Its shape has evolved through the centuries, as documented in many well-known paintings. Its form, topped by a likeness of the Doge's hat, became gradually standardized, and was then fixed by local law. It consists of six bars pointing forward representing the Sestieri of the city, and one that points backward representing the <a href="/wiki/Giudecca" title="Giudecca">Giudecca</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg/220px-Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg/330px-Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg/440px-Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5029" data-file-height="2799" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialtobr%C3%BCcke_am_Tag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice is a city of small islands, enhanced during the Middle Ages by the dredging of soils to raise the marshy ground above the tides. The resulting canals encouraged the flourishing of a nautical culture which proved central to the economy of the city. Today those canals still provide the means for transport of goods and people within the city.</p>
<p>The maze of canals threaded through the city requires the use of more than 400 bridges to permit the flow of foot traffic. In 2011, the city opened <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Costituzione" title="Ponte della Costituzione">Ponte della Costituzione</a>, the fourth bridge across the Grand Canal, connecting the <a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a> bus terminal area with the Stazione Ferroviaria (train station), the others being the original <a href="/wiki/Ponte_di_Rialto" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponte di Rialto">Ponte di Rialto</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_dell%27Accademia" title="Ponte dell'Accademia">Ponte dell'Accademia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_degli_Scalzi" title="Ponte degli Scalzi">Ponte degli Scalzi</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Azienda_del_Consorzio_Trasporti_Veneziano" class="mw-redirect" title="Azienda del Consorzio Trasporti Veneziano">Azienda del Consorzio Trasporti Veneziano</a> (ACTV) is a public company responsible for public transportation in Venice.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lagoon_area">Lagoon area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Lagoon area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The main public transportation means are motorised <a href="/wiki/Waterbus" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterbus">waterbuses</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Vaporetto" title="Vaporetto">vaporetti</a></i>) which ply regular routes along the Grand Canal and between the city's islands. The only gondole still in common use by Venetians are the <i>traghetti</i>, foot passenger <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a> crossing the Grand Canal at certain points without bridges.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_People_Mover" title="Venice People Mover">Venice People Mover</a> (managed by ASM) is a <a href="/wiki/Cable_railway" title="Cable railway">cable</a>-operated <a href="/wiki/Public_transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Public transit">public transit</a> system connecting <a href="/wiki/Tronchetto_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Tronchetto island">Tronchetto island</a> with Piazzale Roma. Water taxis are also active.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lido_and_Pellestrina_islands">Lido and Pellestrina islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lido and Pellestrina islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pellestrina" title="Pellestrina">Pellestrina</a> are two islands forming a barrier between the southern Venetian Lagoon and the Adriatic Sea. In those islands, road traffic is allowed. There are bus services on islands and waterbus services linking islands with other islands (Venice, <a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burano" title="Burano">Burano</a>) and with the peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Cavallino-Treporti" title="Cavallino-Treporti">Cavallino-Treporti</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland">Mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The mainland of Venice is composed of 5 boroughs: <a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a>-Carpenedo, <a href="/wiki/Marghera" title="Marghera">Marghera</a>, Chirignago-Zelarino and Favaro Veneto. Mestre is the center and the most populated urban area of the mainland of Venice. There are several bus routes and two <a href="/wiki/Translohr" title="Translohr">Translohr</a> <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Mestre" title="Trams in Mestre">tramway lines</a>. Several bus routes and one of the above tramway lines link the mainland with <i><a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a></i>, the main bus station in Venice, via <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Libert%C3%A0" title="Ponte della Libertà">Ponte della Libertà</a>, a road bridge connecting the mainland with the group of islands that comprise the historic center of Venice.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trains">Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Venice has regional and national trains, including trains to Rome (3.5 hours) and Milan (2.5 hours). Treviso is 35 minutes away.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Florence and Padua are two of the stops between Rome and Venice. There are two main stations:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_railway_station" title="Venezia Santa Lucia railway station">St Lucia station</a> is a few steps away from a vaporetti stop in the historic city next to <i>Piazzale Roma</i>. As well as many more local trains, this station is the terminus of the Venice Simplon Orient Express from Paris and London.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Mestre_railway_station" title="Venezia Mestre railway station">Mestre station</a> is on the mainland, on the border between the boroughs of Mestre and Marghera.</li>
</ul>
<p>Both stations are managed by Grandi Stazioni; they are linked by the <i>Ponte della Libertà</i> (Liberty Bridge) between the mainland and the islands.</p>
<p>Others small stations in the municipality are: Venezia Porto Marghera, Venezia Carpenedo, Venezia Mestre Ospedale, Venezia Mestre Porta Ovest.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG/220px-Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG/330px-Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG/440px-Morning_Impression_along_a_Canal_in_Venice.JPG 2x" data-file-width="559" data-file-height="747" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Venice is served by the <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Marco Polo International Airport">Marco Polo International Airport</a> (<i>Aeroporto di Venezia <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a></i>), named in honor of its noted citizen. The airport is on the mainland and was rebuilt away from the coast. Public transport from the airport takes one to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Venice <a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a> by ATVO (provincial company) buses<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and by ACTV (city company) buses (route 5 <i>aerobus</i>);<sup id="cite_ref-actv.it_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actv.it-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li>Venice, Lido and Murano by Alilaguna (private company) motor boats;</li>
<li>Mestre, the mainland and Venice Mestre railway station (convenient for connections to <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Padova" class="mw-redirect" title="Padova">Padova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a> and the rest of Italy) by ACTV lines (route 15 and 45)<sup id="cite_ref-actv.it_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actv.it-54">[54]</a></sup> and by ATVO lines;</li>
<li>regional destinations (Treviso, Padua, the beach, ...) by ATVO buses and by Busitalia Sita Nord<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> buses (national company).</li>
</ul>
<p>Some airlines market <a href="/wiki/Treviso_Airport" title="Treviso Airport">Treviso Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Treviso" title="Treviso">Treviso</a>, 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) from Venice, as a Venice gateway. Some simply advertise flights to "Venice", while naming the actual airport only in small print.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> There are public buses from the airport to Venice from this airport.</p>
<p>Venezia-Lido "Giovanni Nicelli",<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> a public airport suitable for smaller aircraft, is at the NE end of <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido di Venezia</a>. It has a 994-metre grass runway.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The main football club in the city is <a href="/wiki/FBC_Unione_Venezia" class="mw-redirect" title="FBC Unione Venezia">FBC Unione Venezia</a>, founded in 1907, who currently plays in the <a href="/wiki/Lega_Pro_Prima_Divisione" title="Lega Pro Prima Divisione">Lega Pro Prima Divisione</a>. Their ground, the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Pierluigi_Penzo" title="Stadio Pierluigi Penzo">Stadio Pierluigi Penzo</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Elena" title="Sant'Elena">Sant'Elena</a>, is one of the oldest venues in Italy.</p>
<p>The local basketball team, <a href="/wiki/Reyer_Venezia_Mestre" title="Reyer Venezia Mestre">Reyer Venezia Mestre</a>, plays in the first national league, the <a href="/wiki/Lega_Basket_Serie_A" title="Lega Basket Serie A">Lega Basket Serie A</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Venice is a major international centre for higher education. The city hosts the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Foscari_University_of_Venice" title="Ca' Foscari University of Venice">Ca' Foscari University of Venice</a>, founded in 1868;<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_Iuav_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="University Iuav of Venice">IUAV University of Venice</a>, founded in 1926;<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Venice_International_University" title="Venice International University">Venice International University</a>, an international research center, founded in 1995 and located on the island of <a href="/wiki/San_Servolo" title="San Servolo">San Servolo</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and the EIUC-European Inter-University Centre for Human Rights and Democratisation, located on the island of Lido di Venezia.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other Venetian institutions of higher education are: the "Accademia di Belle Arti" (Academy of Fine Arts), established in 1750, whose first Chairman was <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Piazzetta" title="Giovanni Battista Piazzetta">Giovanni Battista Piazzetta</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and the "<a href="/wiki/Benedetto_Marcello" title="Benedetto Marcello">Benedetto Marcello</a>" Conservatory of Music, which, established in 1876 as High School and Musical Society, later (1915) became "Liceo Musicale" and finally (1940), when its Director was <a href="/wiki/Gian_Francesco_Malipiero" title="Gian Francesco Malipiero">Gian Francesco Malipiero</a>, State Conservatory of Music.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The city was one of the largest in Europe in the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, with a population of 60,000 in AD 1000; 80,000 in 1200; and rising up to 110,000–180,000 in 1300. In the mid 1500s the city's population was 170,000, and by 1600 almost 200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, there were 270,098 people residing in Venice's comune (the population estimate of 272,000 inhabitants includes the population of the whole Comune of Venezia; around 60,000 in the historic city of Venice (Centro storico); 176,000 in Terraferma (the Mainland); and 31,000 live on other islands in the lagoon), of whom 47.4% were male and 52.6% were female. Minors (children ages 18 and younger) were 14.36% of the population compared to pensioners who numbered 25.7%. This compared with the Italian average of 18.06% (minors) and 19.94% (pensioners). The average age of Venice residents was 46 compared to the Italian average of 42. In the five years between 2002 and 2007, the population of Venice declined by 0.2%, while Italy as a whole grew by 3.85%.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The population in the historic old city declined much faster: from about 120,000 in 1980 to about 60,000 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 91% of the population was Italian. The largest immigrant group came from other European nations: (<a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, the largest group: 3%, South Asia: 1.3%, and East Asia: 0.9%).</p>
<p>Venice is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (92.7% of resident population in the area of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Venice" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Venice">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Venice</a> in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>), but because of the long-standing relationship with <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, there is also a noticeable <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Orthodox</a> presence, and as a result of immigration, there are now some Muslim, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> inhabitants. There is also a historic <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Community_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Community of Venice">Jewish community</a> in Venice. The <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Ghetto" title="Venetian Ghetto">Venetian Ghetto</a> was the area in which Jews were compelled to live under the Venetian Republic. The word <i>ghetto</i>, originally <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a>, is now used in many languages. <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merchant_of_Venice" title="The Merchant of Venice">The Merchant of Venice</a></i>, written in the late 16th century, features <a href="/wiki/Shylock" title="Shylock">Shylock</a>, a Venetian Jew. The first complete and uncensored printed edition of the <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Talmud</a> was printed in Venice by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bomberg" title="Daniel Bomberg">Daniel Bomberg</a> in 1523. In more modern times, Venice has an <a href="/wiki/Eruv" title="Eruv">eruv</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> used by the Jewish community.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema.2C_media.2C_and_popular_culture">Cinema, media, and popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cinema, media, and popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venice_in_media" title="Venice in media">Venice in media</a></div>
<p>Venice has been the setting or chosen location of numerous films, games, works of literature, music videos, novels, poems, television shows, and other cultural references.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_literature_and_adapted_works">In literature and adapted works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: In literature and adapted works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city is a particularly popular setting for essays, novels, and other works of fictional or non-fictional literature. Examples of these include: <a href="/wiki/Casanova" class="mw-redirect" title="Casanova">Casanova</a>'s autobiographical <i>History of My Life</i>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Jonson" title="Ben Jonson">Ben Jonson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Volpone" title="Volpone">Volpone</a></i> (1605-6), <a href="/wiki/Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice">Anne Rice</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Cry_to_Heaven" title="Cry to Heaven">Cry to Heaven</a></i> (1982), <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Merchant_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant of Venice">Merchant of Venice</a></i> (ca. 1596–1598) and <i><a href="/wiki/Othello" title="Othello">Othello</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Sollers" title="Philippe Sollers">Philippe Sollers</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Watteau_in_Venice" title="Watteau in Venice">Watteau in Venice</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Candide" title="Candide">Candide</a></i>. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a>'s novella, <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice" title="Death in Venice">Death in Venice</a></i> (1912), was the basis for Benjamin Britten's opera <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice_(opera)" title="Death in Venice (opera)">Death in Venice</a></i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<li>Three <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> films: <i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia_with_Love_(film)" title="From Russia with Love (film)">From Russia with Love</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(film)" title="Moonraker (film)">Moonraker</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> (2006)</li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_games">In games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: In games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city is the setting for such video games as <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_II" title="Assassin's Creed II">Assassin's Creed II</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tomb_Raider_II" title="Tomb Raider II">Tomb Raider II</a></i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_music">In music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: In music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city has been the setting for the music videos of <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees" title="Siouxsie and the Banshees">Siouxsie and the Banshees</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Dear_Prudence#Cover_versions" title="Dear Prudence">Dear Prudence</a>" .</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Gothic_architecture" title="Venetian Gothic architecture">Venetian Gothic architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/8th_International_Architecture_Exhibition" title="8th International Architecture Exhibition">8th International Architecture Exhibition</a>, <a href="/wiki/9th_International_Architecture_Exhibition" title="9th International Architecture Exhibition">9th International Architecture Exhibition</a>, <a href="/wiki/10th_International_Architecture_Exhibition" title="10th International Architecture Exhibition">10th International Architecture Exhibition</a>, and <a href="/wiki/11th_International_Architecture_Exhibition" title="11th International Architecture Exhibition">11th International Architecture Exhibition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_Rezzonico_(Venice).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/220px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/330px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/440px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5904" data-file-height="3922" /></a>

<div class="thumb tleft">
