</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg/220px-Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg" width="220" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg/330px-Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg/440px-Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1147" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro-la-fenice-sala.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/La_Fenice" title="La Fenice">La Fenice</a> operahouse in the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice has a rich and diverse <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural style</a>, the most prominent of which is the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> style. <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Gothic_architecture" title="Venetian Gothic architecture">Venetian Gothic architecture</a> is a term given to a Venetian building style combining use of the Gothic lancet arch with <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman</a> influences. The style originated in 14th-century Venice, where the confluence of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> style from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> met Arab influence from <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorish Spain">Moorish Spain</a>. Chief examples of the style are the <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace,_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Doge's Palace, Venice">Doge's Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_d%27Oro" title="Ca' d'Oro">Ca' d'Oro</a> in the city. The city also has several <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> buildings, including the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Pesaro" title="Ca' Pesaro">Ca' Pesaro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Rezzonico" title="Ca' Rezzonico">Ca' Rezzonico</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Venice" title="Music of Venice">Music of Venice</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_polychoral_style" title="Venetian polychoral style">Venetian polychoral style</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Veneto" title="Music of Veneto">Music of Veneto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(music)" title="Venetian School (music)">Venetian School (music)</a></div>
<p>The city of Venice in Italy has played an important role in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Italy" title="Music of Italy">music of Italy</a>. The Venetian state – i.e., the medieval <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maritime_Republic_of_Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maritime Republic of Venice (page does not exist)">Maritime Republic of Venice</a> – was often popularly called the "Republic of Music", and an anonymous Frenchman of the 17th century is said to have remarked that "In every home, someone is playing a musical instrument or singing. There is music everywhere."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 16th century, Venice became one of the most important musical centers of Europe, marked by a characteristic style of composition (the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(music)" title="Venetian School (music)">Venetian school</a>) and the development of the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_polychoral_style" title="Venetian polychoral style">Venetian polychoral style</a> under composers such as <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Willaert" title="Adrian Willaert">Adrian Willaert</a>, who worked at <a href="/wiki/San_Marco_di_Venezia" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marco di Venezia">St Mark's Basilica</a>. Venice was the early center of music printing; <a href="/wiki/Ottaviano_Petrucci" title="Ottaviano Petrucci">Ottaviano Petrucci</a> began publishing music almost as soon as this technology was available, and his publishing enterprise helped to attract composers from all over Europe, especially from France and <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>. By the end of the century, Venice was known for the splendor of its music, as exemplified in the "colossal style" of <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gabrieli" title="Andrea Gabrieli">Andrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gabrieli" title="Giovanni Gabrieli">Giovanni Gabrieli</a>, which used multiple choruses and instrumental groups. Venice was also the home of many noted composers during the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque period</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Antonio Vivaldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ippolito_Ciera" title="Ippolito Ciera">Ippolito Ciera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Picchi" title="Giovanni Picchi">Giovanni Picchi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Dalla_Casa" title="Girolamo Dalla Casa">Girolamo Dalla Casa</a>, to name but a few.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interior_design">Interior design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Interior design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It can be argued that Venice produced the best and most refined <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">rococo</a> designs. At the time<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, Venice was in trouble. It had lost most of its maritime power, was lagging behind its rivals in political importance, and society had become decadent, with nobles wasting their money in gambling and partying. But Venice remained Italy's fashion capital, and was a serious contender to Paris in terms of wealth, architecture, luxury, taste, sophistication, trade, decoration, style, and design.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_2005_p.82_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller_2005_p.82-75">[75]</a></sup> Venetian rococo was well known as rich and luxurious, with usually very extravagant designs. Unique Venetian furniture pieces included the <i>divani da portego</i>, and long rococo couches and <i>pozzetti</i>, objects meant to be placed against the wall. Bedrooms of rich Venetians were usually sumptuous and grand, with rich damask, velvet, and silk drapery and curtains, and beautifully carved rococo beds with statues of <a href="/wiki/Putti" class="mw-redirect" title="Putti">putti</a>, flowers and angels.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_2005_p.82_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller_2005_p.82-75">[75]</a></sup> Venice was especially known for its beautiful <a href="/w/index.php?title=Girandole_mirrors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Girandole mirrors (page does not exist)">girandole mirrors</a>, which remained among, if not the, finest in Europe. Chandeliers were usually very colourful, using <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a> to make them look more vibrant and stand out from others, and precious stones and materials from abroad were used, since Venice still held a vast trade empire. Lacquer was very common, and many items of furniture were covered with it, the most noted being <i>lacca povera</i> (poor lacquer), in which allegories and images of social life were painted. Lacquerwork and <a href="/wiki/Chinoiserie" title="Chinoiserie">Chinoiserie</a> were particularly common in bureau cabinets.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion_and_shopping">Fashion and shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Fashion and shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG/170px-Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG/255px-Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG/340px-Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialto_IMG_3996.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Luxury shops and boutiques along the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 14th century, many young Venetian men began wearing tight-fitting multicoloured hose, the designs on which indicated the Compagnie della Calza ("Trouser Club") to which they belonged. The Venetian Senate passed <a href="/wiki/Sumptuary_law" title="Sumptuary law">sumptuary laws</a>, but these merely resulted in changes in fashion in order to circumvent the law. Dull garments were worn over colourful ones, which then were cut to show the hidden colours resulting in the wide spread of men's "slashed" fashions in the 15th century.</p>
<p>Today, Venice is a major fashion and shopping centre, not as important as <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, and Rome, but on a par with <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicenza" title="Vicenza">Vicenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roberta_di_Camerino" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberta di Camerino">Roberta di Camerino</a> is the only major <a href="/wiki/Italian_fashion" title="Italian fashion">Italian fashion</a> brand to be based in Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-77">[77]</a></sup> Founded in 1945, it is renowned for its innovative handbags featuring hardware<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> by Venetian artisans and often covered in locally woven velvet, and has been credited with creating the concept of the easily recognisable <a href="/wiki/It_bag" class="mw-redirect" title="It bag">status bag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-77">[77]</a></sup> Many of the fashion boutiques and jewelry shops in the city are located on or near the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>. There are <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ermenegildo_Zegna" title="Ermenegildo Zegna">Ermenegildo Zegna</a> flagship stores in the city. If shopping for venetian and Italian food specialties and wine you can head to Mascari or Casa del Parmigiano near Rialto and <a href="/w/index.php?title=I_Tre_Mercanti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="I Tre Mercanti (page does not exist)">I Tre Mercanti</a> flagship store near <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian cuisine">Venetian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venetian_wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian wine">Venetian wine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg/170px-Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg/255px-Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg/340px-Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2536" data-file-height="3286" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pietro_Longhi_025.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hot chocolate was a fashionable drink in Venice during the 1770s and 1780s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venetian cuisine is characterized by seafood, but also includes garden products from the islands of the lagoon, rice from the mainland, game, and <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>. Venice combines local traditions with influences stemming from age-old contacts with distant countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These include <i>sarde in saór</i> (sardines marinated to preserve them for long voyages); <i>bacalà mantecato</i> (a recipe based on Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Stockfish" title="Stockfish">stockfish</a> and extra-virgin olive oil); <i>bisàto</i> (marinated eel); <i>risi e bisi</i>, rice, peas and (not smoked) bacon;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <i>fegato alla veneziana</i>, Venetian-style veal liver; <i>risòto col néro de sépe</i> (risotto with cuttlefish, blackened by their ink); <i>cicchétti</i>, refined and delicious tidbits (akin to <i>tapas</i>); <i>antipasti</i> (appetizers); and <i><a href="/wiki/Prosecco" title="Prosecco">prosecco</a></i>, an effervescent, mildly sweet wine.</p>
<p>In addition, Venice is known for the golden, oval-shaped cookies called <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ba%C3%ACcoli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baìcoli (page does not exist)">baìcoli</a></i>, and for other types of sweets, such as: <i>pan del pescatore</i> (bread of the fisherman); cookies with almonds and pistachio nuts; cookies with fried Venetian cream, or the <i>bussolài</i> (<a href="/wiki/Butter_biscuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Butter biscuit">butter biscuits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortbread" title="Shortbread">shortbread</a> made in the shape of a ring or of an "S") from the island of Burano; the <i>galàni</i> or <i>cróstoli</i> (<a href="/wiki/Angel_wings" title="Angel wings">angel wings</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> the <i>frìtole</i> (spherical doughnuts); the <i>fregolòtta</i> (a crumbly cake with almonds); a milk pudding called <i>rosada</i>; and cookies called <i>zaléti</i>, whose ingredients include yellow maize flour.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dessert <a href="/wiki/Tiramis%C3%B9" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiramisù">tiramisù</a> is thought to have been invented in <a href="/wiki/Treviso" title="Treviso">Treviso</a> in the late 1960s, and is popular in the <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> area.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_literature" title="Venetian literature">Venetian literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casanova_ritratto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Casanova_ritratto.jpg/170px-Casanova_ritratto.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Casanova_ritratto.jpg/255px-Casanova_ritratto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Casanova_ritratto.jpg/340px-Casanova_ritratto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1111" data-file-height="1429" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casanova_ritratto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of Giacomo Casanova.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice has long been a source of inspiration for authors, poets and playwrights as well as being at the forefront of the technical developing of printing and publishing.</p>
<p>Two of the most noted Venetian writers were <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> in the Middle Ages and later <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a>. Polo (1254–1324) was a merchant who voyaged to <a href="/wiki/The_Orient" class="mw-redirect" title="The Orient">the Orient</a>. His series of books, co-written by <a href="/wiki/Rustichello_da_Pisa" title="Rustichello da Pisa">Rustichello da Pisa</a>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">Il Milione</a></i> provided important knowledge of the lands east of Europe, from the Middle East to China, Japan and Russia. <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a> (1725–1798) was a prolific writer and adventurer best remembered for his autobiography, <i>Histoire De Ma Vie</i> (Story of My Life), which links his colourful lifestyle to the city of Venice.</p>
<p>Venetian playwrights followed the old Italian theatre tradition of <i><a href="/wiki/Commedia_dell%27arte" title="Commedia dell'arte">Commedia dell'arte</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Angelo_Beolco" title="Angelo Beolco">Ruzante</a> (1502–1542), <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a> (1707–1793) and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Gozzi" title="Carlo Gozzi">Carlo Gozzi</a> (1720–1806) used the Venetian dialect extensively in their comedies.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aldus-Horace2.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Aldus-Horace2.jpeg/220px-Aldus-Horace2.jpeg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Aldus-Horace2.jpeg/330px-Aldus-Horace2.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Aldus-Horace2.jpeg/440px-Aldus-Horace2.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aldus-Horace2.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
book printed by Aldus Manutius.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice has also inspired writers from abroad. Shakespeare set <i><a href="/wiki/Othello" title="Othello">Othello</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merchant_of_Venice" title="The Merchant of Venice">The Merchant of Venice</a></i> in the city. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a> wrote the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice" title="Death in Venice">Death in Venice</a></i>, published in 1912. Venice inspired the poetry of <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Pound" title="Ezra Pound">Ezra Pound</a>, who wrote his first literary work in the city. Pound died in 1972 and his remains are buried in Venice's cemetery island of <a href="/wiki/Isola_di_San_Michele" title="Isola di San Michele">San Michele</a>. The French writer <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Sollers" title="Philippe Sollers">Philippe Sollers</a> spent most of his life in Venice and published <i>A Dictionary For Lovers Of Venice</i> in 2004. <a href="/wiki/Ugo_Foscolo" title="Ugo Foscolo">Ugo Foscolo</a> (1778–1827), born in <a href="/wiki/Zakynthos" title="Zakynthos">Zante</a>, an island that at the time belonged to the Republic of Venice, was also a poet and <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a> who wanted to see a free republic established in Venice following its fall to <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>. The city features prominently in Henry James' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aspern_Papers" title="The Aspern Papers">The Aspern Papers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wings_of_the_Dove" title="The Wings of the Dove">The Wings of the Dove</a></i>, and is also visited in <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Evelyn Waugh</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Brideshead_Revisited" title="Brideshead Revisited">Brideshead Revisited</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Proust" title="Marcel Proust">Marcel Proust</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/In_Search_of_Lost_Time" title="In Search of Lost Time">In Search of Lost Time</a></i>. Perhaps the most known children's book set in Venice is <i>The Thief Lord</i>, written by the German author <a href="/wiki/Cornelia_Funke" title="Cornelia Funke">Cornelia Funke</a>.</p>
<p>Venice is also linked to the technological aspects of writing. The city was the location of one of Italy's earliest printing presses, established by <a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a> (1449–1515).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> From this beginning Venice developed as an important typographic center and even as late as the 18th century was responsible for printing half of Italy's published books.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_printing">Art and printing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Art and printing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_painters_and_architects_of_Venice" title="List of painters and architects of Venice">List of painters and architects of Venice</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian School (art)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg/220px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg/330px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg/440px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="569" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_From_the_Gondola_-_John_Singer_Sargent.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>From the Gondola</i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Singer_Sargent" title="John Singer Sargent">John Singer Sargent</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="30000" data-file-height="20857" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An 18th-century view of Venice by Venetian artist <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> periods, was a major centre of art and developed a unique style known as the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian School</a>. In the Middle Ages and the Renaissance, Venice, along with <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> and Rome, became one of the most important centres of art in Europe, and numerous wealthy Venetians became patrons of the arts. Venice at the time was a rich and prosperous <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Republics">Maritime Republic</a>, which controlled a vast sea and trade empire.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the 15th century, Venice had become the European capital of printing, being one of the first cities in Italy (after Subiaco and Rome) to have a printing press after those established in Germany, having 417 printers by 1500. The most important printing office was the <a href="/wiki/Aldine_Press" title="Aldine Press">Aldine Press</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a>, which in 1499 printed the <i><a href="/wiki/Hypnerotomachia_Poliphili" title="Hypnerotomachia Poliphili">Hypnerotomachia Poliphili</a></i>, considered the most beautiful book of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, and established modern <a href="/wiki/Punctuation" title="Punctuation">punctuation</a>, the page format and <a href="/wiki/Italic_type" title="Italic type">italic type</a>, and the first printed work of <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>.</p>
<p>In the 16th century, Venetian painting was developed through influences from the Paduan School and <a href="/wiki/Antonello_da_Messina" title="Antonello da Messina">Antonello da Messina</a>, who introduced the oil painting technique of the <a href="/wiki/Van_Eyck" title="Van Eyck">Van Eyck</a> brothers. It is signified by a warm colour scale and a picturesque use of colour. Early masters were the Bellini and Vivarini families, followed by <a href="/wiki/Giorgione" title="Giorgione">Giorgione</a> and <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Veronese" title="Paolo Veronese">Veronese</a>. In the early 16th century, there was rivalry in Venetian painting between the <i>disegno</i> and <i>colorito</i> techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Canvas" title="Canvas">Canvases</a> (the common painting surface) originated in Venice during the early Renaissance. These early canvases were generally rough.</p>
<p>In the 18th century, Venetian painting had a revival with <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Tiepolo" title="Giovanni Battista Tiepolo">Tiepolo</a>'s decorative painting and <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Guardi" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardi">Guardi</a>'s panoramic views.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glass">Glass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Glass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glassvenetian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Glassvenetian.jpg/170px-Glassvenetian.jpg" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Glassvenetian.jpg/255px-Glassvenetian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/24/Glassvenetian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="315" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glassvenetian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a> <a href="/wiki/Goblet" class="mw-redirect" title="Goblet">goblet</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venice is known for its ornate glass-work, known as <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a>. It is world-renowned for being colourful, elaborate, and skilfully made.</p>
<p>Many of the important characteristics of these objects had been developed by the 13th century. Toward the end of that century, the center of the Venetian glass industry moved to <a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a>, an offshore island in Venice. The glass made there is known as <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a>.</p>
<p>Byzantine craftsmen played an important role in the development of Venetian glass, an art form for which the city is well known. When <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> was sacked in the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a> in 1204, some fleeing artisans came to Venice. This happened again when the <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> took Constantinople in 1453, supplying Venice with still more glassworkers. By the 16th century, Venetian artisans had gained even greater control over the color and transparency of their glass, and had mastered a variety of decorative techniques.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_compagni,_salone,_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG/170px-Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG/255px-Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG/340px-Palazzo_compagni%2C_salone%2C_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_compagni,_salone,_lampadario_di_murano_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An ornate <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a> <a href="/wiki/Chandelier" title="Chandelier">chandelier</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite efforts to keep Venetian glassmaking techniques within Venice, they became known elsewhere, and Venetian-style glassware was produced in other Italian cities and other countries of Europe.</p>
<p>Some of the most important brands of glass in the world today are still produced in the historical glass factories on Murano. They are: Venini, Barovier &amp; Toso, <a href="/wiki/Pauly_%26_C._-_Compagnia_Venezia_Murano" class="mw-redirect" title="Pauly &amp; C. - Compagnia Venezia Murano">Pauly</a>, Millevetri, Seguso.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Barovier &amp; Toso is considered one of the 100 <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_companies" title="List of oldest companies">oldest companies</a> in the world, formed in 1295.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg/220px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg/330px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg/440px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2359" data-file-height="1769" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnevale_di_Venezia_20100212.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Masks at Carnival of Venice.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a> is held annually in the city, It lasts for around two weeks and ends on <a href="/wiki/Shrove_Tuesday" title="Shrove Tuesday">Shrove Tuesday</a>. <a href="/wiki/Venetian_mask" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian mask">Venetian masks</a> are worn.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_Biennale" title="Venice Biennale">Venice Biennale</a> is one of the most important events in the arts calendar. In 1895 an <i>Esposizione biennale artistica nazionale</i> (biennial exhibition of Italian art) was inaugurated.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The activities of the Biennale were interrupted by the war in September 1942, but resumed in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Festa_del_Redentore" title="Festa del Redentore">Festa del Redentore</a> is held in mid July. It began as a feast to give thanks for the end of the plague of 1576. A bridge of barges is built connecting Giudecca to the rest of Venice, and fireworks play an important role.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a> (<span style="font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" title="in Italian"><a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a></span> <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Mostra Internazionale d'Arte Cinematografica di Venezia</i></span>) is the oldest film festival in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Founded by Count <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Volpi_di_Misurata" class="mw-redirect" title="Giuseppe Volpi di Misurata">Giuseppe Volpi di Misurata</a> in 1932 as the <i>Esposizione Internazionale d'Arte Cinematografica</i>, the festival has since taken place every year in late August or early September on the island of the <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a>. Screenings take place in the historic <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_del_Cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo del Cinema">Palazzo del Cinema</a> on the Lungomare Marconi. It is one of the world's most prestigious film festivals and is part of the Venice Biennale.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_words_of_Venetian_origin">Foreign words of Venetian origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Foreign words of Venetian origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some words with a Venetian etymology include <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/arsenal" class="extiw" title="wikt:arsenal">arsenal</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ciao" class="extiw" title="wikt:ciao">ciao</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ghetto" class="extiw" title="wikt:ghetto">ghetto</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gondola" class="extiw" title="wikt:gondola">gondola</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/imbroglio" class="extiw" title="wikt:imbroglio">imbroglio</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lagoon" class="extiw" title="wikt:lagoon">lagoon</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lazaret" class="extiw" title="wikt:lazaret">lazaret</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lido" class="extiw" title="wikt:lido">lido</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Montenegro" class="extiw" title="wikt:Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quarantine" class="extiw" title="wikt:quarantine">quarantine</a>, and <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/regatta" class="extiw" title="wikt:regatta">regatta</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The name "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Venezuela" class="extiw" title="wikt:Venezuela">Venezuela</a>" is a Spanish diminutive of Venice.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many additional places around the world are named after Venice, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Los_Angeles" title="Venice, Los Angeles">Venice, Los Angeles</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Venice_Beach,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Venice Beach, California">Venice Beach, California</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help improve this section by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(February 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>For people from Venice, see <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Venice" title="Category:People from Venice">Category:People from Venice</a>.</i> Others closely associated with the city include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Cesare_Alberti" class="mw-redirect" title="Pietro Cesare Alberti">Pietro Cesare Alberti</a> (1608–1655), considered the first Italian-American, arriving in New Amsterdam in 1635.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tomaso_Albinoni" title="Tomaso Albinoni">Tomaso Albinoni</a> (8 June 1671 – 17 January 1751), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ambrosini" title="Claudio Ambrosini">Claudio Ambrosini</a> (9 April 1948), composer and conductor.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Bembo" title="Pietro Bembo">Pietro Bembo</a> (20 May 1470 – 18 January 1547), <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Cardinal" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Cardinal">cardinal</a> and scholar.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bellini" title="Giovanni Bellini">Giovanni Bellini</a> (c. 1430–1516), a Renaissance painter, probably the best known of the Bellini family of painters.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Borgato" title="Francesco Borgato">Francesco Borgato</a> (5 September 1990, Venice), is an Italian recording artist and dancer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Antonio_Bragadin" title="Marco Antonio Bragadin">Marco Antonio Bragadin</a> (d.1571), general, flayed alive by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a> after a fierce resistance during the siege of <a href="/wiki/Famagusta" title="Famagusta">Famagusta</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Cabot_(explorer)" title="Sebastian Cabot (explorer)">Sebastian Cabot</a> (c. 1484–1557, or soon after), <a href="/wiki/List_of_explorers" title="List of explorers">explorer</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalba_Carriera" title="Rosalba Carriera">Rosalba Carriera</a> (7 October 1675 – 15 April 1757), known for her pastel works.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a> (28 October 1697 – 19 April 1768), known for his landscapes or <i><a href="/wiki/Veduta" title="Veduta">vedute</a></i> of Venice, but not only.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a> (1725–1798 in <a href="/wiki/Duchcov" title="Duchcov">Dux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, (now <a href="/wiki/Duchcov" title="Duchcov">Duchcov</a>, Czech Republic)), a Venetian adventurer, writer and <a href="/wiki/Womanizing" class="mw-redirect" title="Womanizing">womanizer</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Cavalli" title="Francesco Cavalli">Francesco Cavalli</a> (14 February 1602 – 14 January 1676), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Da_Ponte" title="Lorenzo Da Ponte">Lorenzo Da Ponte</a> (1749–1838), opera librettist and poet. He wrote the librettos for 28 operas by 11 composers, including <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Enrico_Dandolo" title="Enrico Dandolo">Enrico Dandolo</a> (<i>c</i>. 1107, 1205), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 1192 to his death. He played a direct role in the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Constantinople" class="mw-redirect" title="Sack of Constantinople">Sack of Constantinople</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Dandolo" title="Vincenzo Dandolo">Vincenzo Dandolo</a> (1758–1819), chemist, agronomist and politician of the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlightenment Era">Enlightenment Era</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludovico_de_Luigi" title="Ludovico de Luigi">Ludovico de Luigi</a> (November 1933), Venetian Surrealistic artist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pellegrino_Ernetti" title="Pellegrino Ernetti">Pellegrino Ernetti</a>, Catholic priest and exorcist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Veronica_Franco" title="Veronica Franco">Veronica Franco</a> (1546–1591), poet and courtesan during the Renaissance.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gabrieli" title="Andrea Gabrieli">Andrea Gabrieli</a> (c. 1510–1586), Italian composer and organist at St Mark's Basilica.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gabrieli" title="Giovanni Gabrieli">Giovanni Gabrieli</a> (between 1554 and 1557–1612), composer and organist at St Mark's Basilica.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a> (25 February 1707 – 6 February 1793). Along with <a href="/wiki/Pirandello" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirandello">Pirandello</a>, Goldoni is probably the most notable name in Italian theatre, in his country and abroad.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Gozzi" title="Carlo Gozzi">Carlo Gozzi</a> (13 December 1720 – 4 April 1806), an excellent dramatist of the 18th century.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Guarneri" title="Pietro Guarneri">Pietro Guarneri</a> (14 April 1695 – 7 April 1762) left Cremona in 1718, settled in Venice. "Peter of Venice" from the family of great luthiers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baldassare_Longhena" title="Baldassare Longhena">Baldassare Longhena</a> (1598 – 18 February 1682), one of the greatest exponents of Baroque architecture.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Lotto" title="Lorenzo Lotto">Lorenzo Lotto</a> (c. 1480 – Loreto, 1556), painter, draughtsman, and illustrator, traditionally placed in the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian school</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Maderna" title="Bruno Maderna">Bruno Maderna</a> (21 April 1920 – 13 November 1973), an Italian-German orchestra director and 20th-century music composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diogo_Mainardi" title="Diogo Mainardi">Diogo Mainardi</a> (22 September 1962, São Paulo), is a Brazilian writer, journalist and TV commentator.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a> (1449–1515), one of the most important printers in history.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leon_Modena" class="mw-redirect" title="Leon Modena">Leon Modena</a> (1571–1648) preacher, author, poet, active in the Venetian ghetto and beyond.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Monteverdi" title="Claudio Monteverdi">Claudio Monteverdi</a> (1567–1643), composer, opera pioneer, and director of music at <a href="/wiki/San_Marco" title="San Marco">San Marco</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luigi_Nono_(composer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luigi Nono (composer)">Luigi Nono</a> (29 January 1924 – 8 May 1990), a leading composer of instrumental and electronic music.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pardo_(rabbi)" title="Joseph Pardo (rabbi)">Joseph Pardo</a> (c. 1561–1619), rabbi and merchant.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elena_Lucrezia_Cornaro_Piscopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia">Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia</a> (5 June 1646 – 26 July 1684), the first woman in the world to receive a doctorate degree.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> (c. 1254 – 8 January 1324), trader and <a href="/wiki/Exploration" title="Exploration">explorer</a>, one of the first Westerners to travel the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> to China. While a prisoner in Genoa, he dictated in the tale of his travels known as <i>Il Milione</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">The Travels of Marco Polo</a></i>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgilio_Ranzato" title="Virgilio Ranzato">Virgilio Ranzato</a> (7 May 1883 – 20 April 1937), composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Rolfe" title="Frederick Rolfe">Frederick Rolfe</a> (22 July 1860 – 25 October 1913), English author of the Venetian novel <i>The Desire and Pursuit of the Whole</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Scarpa" title="Carlo Scarpa">Carlo Scarpa</a> (2 June 1906 – 1978, <a href="/wiki/Sendai,_Miyagi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sendai, Miyagi">Sendai, Japan</a>), an architect with a profound understanding of materials.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romano_Scarpa" title="Romano Scarpa">Romano Scarpa</a> (27 September 1927, Venice – 23 April 2005, Málaga), was one of the most noted Italian creators of Disney comics.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Sinopoli" title="Giuseppe Sinopoli">Giuseppe Sinopoli</a> (2 November 1946 – 20 April 2001), conductor and composer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Tiepolo" title="Giovanni Battista Tiepolo">Giovanni Battista Tiepolo</a> (5 March 1696 – 27 March 1770), the last "Grand Manner" fresco painter from the Venetian Republic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a> (1518 – 31 May 1594), probably the last great painter of Italian Renaissance.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a> (<i>c</i>. 1488–90 – 27 August 1576), leader of the 16th-century Venetian school of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a> (he was born in <a href="/wiki/Cadore" title="Cadore">Pieve di Cadore</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elisabetta_Camin%C3%A8r_Turra" title="Elisabetta Caminèr Turra">Elisabetta Caminèr Turra</a> (1751–1796), writer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emilio_Vedova" title="Emilio Vedova">Emilio Vedova</a> (9 August 1919 – 25 October 2006), one of the most important modern painters of Italy.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastiano_Venier" title="Sebastiano Venier">Sebastiano Venier</a>, (c. 1496 – 3 March 1578), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 11 June 1577 to 1578.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Antonio Vivaldi</a> (4 March 1678, 28 July (or 27), 1741, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>), composer and violinist of the Baroque Era.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The City of Venice and the Central Association of Cities and Communities of Greece (KEDKE) established, in January 2000, in pursuance of the EC Regulations n. 2137/85, the European Economic Interest Grouping (E.E.I.G.) <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> System to promote and realise European projects within transnational cultural and tourist field, particularly referred to the artistic and architectural heritage preservation and safeguard.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Venice is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran"><img alt="Iran" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/35px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/46px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="360" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Shiraz" title="Shiraz">Shiraz</a>, Iran</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan"><img alt="Pakistan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a>, Pakistan, since 1960</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia"><img alt="Indonesia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a>, Indonesia.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>, China, since 1980</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand"><img alt="Thailand" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/35px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/45px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, Thailand</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia"><img alt="Estonia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Estonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Estonia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="630" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>, Estonia</li>

</div>
<p>In 2013, Venice ended the sister city relationship with St. Petersburg in opposition to laws Russia had passed against homosexuals and those who support gay rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Venice_Russia_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venice_Russia-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_agreements">Cooperation agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Cooperation agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Venice has cooperation agreements with the Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, the German city of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, signed on 25 September 1999, and the Turkish city of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, signed on 4 March 1993, within the framework of the 1991 Istanbul Declaration. It is also a Science and Technology Partnership City with <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>, China.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Academic</dt>
</dl>
<div class="refbegin columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><cite class="citation book">Bosio, Luciano. <i>Le origini di Venezia</i>. Novara: Istituto Geografico De Agostini.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenice&amp;rft.aufirst=Luciano&amp;rft.aulast=Bosio&amp;rft.btitle=Le+origini+di+Venezia&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Novara&amp;rft.pub=Istituto+Geografico+De+Agostini&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horatio_Brown" title="Horatio Brown">Brown, Horatio</a>, <i>Venice</i>, chapter 8 of <i><a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Modern_History" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge Modern History">Cambridge Modern History</a></i> vol. I <i>The Renaissance</i> (1902)</li>
<li>Brown, Horatio, <i>Calendar of State Papers (Venetian): 1581–1591</i>, 1895; <i>1592–1603</i>, 1897; <i>1603–1607</i>, 1900; <i>1607–1610</i>, 1904; <i>1610–1613</i>, 1905</li>
<li>Brown, Horatio, <i>Studies in the history of Venice</i> (London, 1907)</li>
<li>Chambers, D.S. (1970). <i>The Imperial Age of Venice, 1380–1580.</i> London: Thames &amp; Hudson. The best brief introduction in English, still completely reliable.</li>
<li>Contarini, Gasparo (1599). <i>The Commonwealth and Gouernment of Venice.</i> Lewes Lewkenor, trsl. London: "Imprinted by I. Windet for E. Mattes." The most important contemporary account of Venice's governance during the time of its blossoming. Also available in various reprint editions.</li>
<li>Da Canal, Martin, "Les estoires de Venise" (13th-century chronicle), translated by Laura Morreale. Padua, Unipress 2009.</li>
<li>Drechsler, Wolfgang (2002). "Venice Misappropriated." <i>Trames</i> 6(2), pp.&#160;192–201. A scathing review of Martin &amp; Romano 2000; also a good summary on the most recent economic and political thought on Venice.</li>
<li>Garrett, Martin, "Venice: a Cultural History" (2006). Revised edition of "Venice: a Cultural and Literary Companion" (2001).</li>
<li>Grubb, James S. (1986). "When Myths Lose Power: Four Decades of Venetian Historiography." <i>Journal of Modern History</i> 58, pp.&#160;43–94. The classic "muckraking" essay on the myths of Venice.</li>
<li>Lane, Frederic Chapin. <i>Venice: Maritime Republic</i> (1973) (<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780801814457" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8018-1445-7</a>) standard scholarly history; emphasis on economic, political and diplomatic history</li>
<li>Laven, Mary, "Virgins of Venice: Enclosed Lives and Broken Vows in the Renaissance Convent (2002). The most important study of the life of Renaissance nuns, with much on aristocratic family networks and the life of women more generally.</li>
<li>Madden, Thomas F. <i>Enrico Dandolo and the Rise of Venice</i> Johns Hopkins University Press. Probably the best book in English on medieval Venice.</li>
<li>Martin, John Jeffries and Dennis Romano (eds). <i>Venice Reconsidered. The History and Civilization of an Italian City-State, 1297–1797.</i> (2002) <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>. The most recent collection on essays, many by prominent scholars, on Venice.</li>
<li>Muir, Edward (1981). <i>Civic Ritual in Renaissance Venice.</i> Princeton UP. The classic of Venetian cultural studies, highly sophisticated.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_J._Oppenheimer" title="Gerald J. Oppenheimer">Oppenheimer, Gerald J.</a> (2010). <i>Venetian</i> Palazzi <i>and</i> Case: <i>A Guide to the Literature.</i> University of Washington, Seattle. Retrieved from <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://faculty.washington.edu/gerryo/venice.html">http://faculty.washington.edu/gerryo/venice.html</a> 7 February 2010.</li>
<li>Rösch, Gerhard (2000). <i>Venedig. Geschichte einer Seerepublik.</i> Stuttgart: Kohlhammer. In German, but the most recent top-level brief history of Venice.</li>
<li><cite class="citation book">Miller, Judith (2005). <i>Furniture: world styles from classical to contemporary</i>. DK Publishing. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7566-1340-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7566-1340-2">978-0-7566-1340-2</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVenice&amp;rft.aufirst=Judith&amp;rft.aulast=Miller&amp;rft.btitle=Furniture%3A+world+styles+from+classical+to+contemporary&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7566-1340-2&amp;rft.pub=DK+Publishing&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<dl>
<dt>Popular</dt>
</dl>
<div class="refbegin columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ackroyd,_Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="Ackroyd, Peter">Ackroyd, Peter</a>. <i>Venice: Pure City</i>. London, Chatto &amp; Windus. 2009. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780701184780" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-7011-8478-0</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horatio_Brown" title="Horatio Brown">Brown, Horatio</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_on_the_Lagoons" title="Life on the Lagoons">Life on the Lagoons</a></i>, 1884; revised ed. 1894; further eds. 1900, 1904, 1909.</li>
<li>Cole, Toby. <i>Venice: A Portable Reader</i>, Lawrence Hill, 1979. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780882080970" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-88208-097-0</a> (hardcover); <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780882081076" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-88208-107-6</a> (softcover).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Madden" title="Thomas Madden">Madden, Thomas</a>, <i>Venice: A New History</i>. New York: Viking, 2012. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780670025428" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-670-02542-8</a>. A fascinating and approachable history by a distinguished historian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jan_Morris" title="Jan Morris">Morris, Jan</a> (1993), <i>Venice</i>. 3rd revised edition. Faber &amp; Faber, <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780571168972" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-571-16897-2</a>. A subjective and passionate written introduction to the city and some of its history. Not illustrated.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Ruskin" title="John Ruskin">Ruskin, John (1853)</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stones_of_Venice_(book)" title="The Stones of Venice (book)">The Stones of Venice</a></i>. Abridged edition Links, JG (Ed), Penguin Books, 2001. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780141390659" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-14-139065-9</a>. Seminal work on architecture and society</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrea_di_Robilant" title="Andrea di Robilant">di Robilant, Andrea</a> (2004). <i>A Venetian Affair</i>. HarperCollins. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781841155425" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-84115-542-5</a> Biography of Venetian nobleman and lover, from correspondence in the 1750s.</li>
<li>Sethre, Janet. <i>The Souls of Venice</i> McFarland &amp; Company, Inc., 2003. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780786415731" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-7864-1573-1</a> (softcover). This book focuses on people who have been shaped by Venice and who have shaped the city in their turn. Illustrated (photographs by Manuela Fardin).</li>
</ul>
